P*c3*exp(P*c4) + P*c5/(c6*exp(P*c7) + 1) + c8", "P**3*c0 + P**2*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3*exp(P*c4)/(c5*exp(P*c4) + 1) + c6/(c7*exp(c8*t) + 1)", "P**3*c0 + P**2*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3/(c4*exp(P*c5) + 1) + c6*t**c7 + c8/(c9 + t)", "P**3*c0 + P**2*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3*exp(P*c4)/(c5*exp(P*c6) + 1) + c7*sin(P*c8 + c9)", "P**3*c0 + P**2*c1 + P**2*c2/(c3*exp(P*c4) + 1) + P*c5 + P*c6/(c3*exp(P*c4) + 1) + c7*exp(P**c8*c9)", "P**3*c0 + P**2*c1 + P**2*c2/(c3*exp(P*c4) + 1) + P*c5 + P*c6/(c3*exp(P*c4) + 1) + c7*t**c8", "P**3*c0 + P**2*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3/(c4*exp(P*c5) + 1) + c6*t**c7", "P**3*c0 + P**2*c1 + P*c2 + P**c3*c4/(c5*exp(P*c6) + 1) + c7*t**c8"]

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

## GT Analysis

The GT is:
```
c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P + c6*P/(c7 + exp(-c8*(-c9 + P)))
```

With numerical values substituted:
```
0.201*(-1 + P/5.637)*(1 - P/10.233)*P + 0.201*P + 0.201*P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(-0.634 + P)))
```

Let me expand the first term:
(-1 + P/5.637)(1 - P/10.233) = -1 + P/10.233 + P/5.637 - P²/(5.637×10.233)

So the first term times 0.201*P gives:
0.201*P*[-1 + P/10.233 + P/5.637 - P²/57.68]

= 0.201*(-P + P²/10.233 + P²/5.637 - P³/57.68)

= -0.201P + 0.201P²(1/10.233 + 1/5.637) - 0.201P³/57.68

Adding 0.201*P cancels the -0.201P term.

So GT = 0.201P²(1/10.233 + 1/5.637) - 0.201P³/57.68 + 0.201P/(1 + exp(-5.637(-0.634 + P)))

This simplifies to:
**GT = aP³ + bP² + cP/(1 + d·exp(-eP))**

where a, b are specific constants and c, d, e are specific constants. Note there's no constant term, no linear P term (they cancelled), and no t dependence.

Let me verify: the linear terms: -0.201P + 0.201P = 0. Correct, no linear P term remains.

So GT has the form: **P³·α + P²·β + P·γ/(δ + exp(εP))**

where α, β are constants and the sigmoid term involves P.

Now let me rewrite the sigmoid term: 0.201P/(1 + exp(-5.637(-0.634+P))) = 0.201P/(1 + exp(5.637·0.634 - 5.637P)) = 0.201P/(1 + exp(3.573)·exp(-5.637P))

So GT = αP³ + βP² + γP/(1 + δ·exp(-εP)) with no other terms.

Now I'll check each candidate for structural equivalence.

**Key structural requirements:**
1. P³ term
2. P² term  
3. P/(1 + c·exp(c·P)) term (sigmoid-like)
4. NO constant term
5. NO linear P term (or it can be absorbed)
6. NO t dependence
7. No other basis functions (sin, cos, etc.)

Wait, let me reconsider. The linear P term cancelled, but a candidate could have a linear P term with coefficient set to 0. Let me re-examine.

Actually, looking more carefully: the GT has P³, P², and P/(sigmoid). A candidate with P³ + P² + P + P/(sigmoid) could work if we set the P coefficient to 0. But a candidate with P³ + P² + P·c2 + P·c3/(sigmoid) - here c2 can be set to 0.

Let me now systematically check candidates:

### Candidate 1: P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + Pc3/(c4·exp(Pc5)+1) + c6 + c7/(c8+t)
Has t-dependent term c7/(c8+t) and constant c6. Can set c7=0 and c6=0. Then: P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + Pc3/(c4·exp(Pc5)+1). Set c2=0. This matches GT structure.
Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 2: P³c0 + P·P^c1·c2 + Pc3/(c4·exp(Pc5)+1) + P^c1·c6 + c7/(c8+t) + c9
Has P^c1 terms (non-integer power), t-dependence. Set c7=0, c9=0, c6=0. Then P³c0 + P·P^c1·c2 + Pc3/(c4·exp(Pc5)+1). Need P·P^c1 = P^(1+c1). Set c1=1 to get P². But then we only have P³ + P² + sigmoid term. That matches if we don't need a separate P² and the structure works. Actually with c1=1: P³c0 + P²c2 + Pc3/(c4·exp(Pc5)+1). This matches GT.
Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 3: P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + Pc3/(c4·exp(Pc5)+1) + c6/(c7+t)
Has t-dependent term c6/(c7+t). Set c6=0. Then P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + Pc3/(c4·exp(Pc5)+1). Set c2=0. Matches GT.
Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 4: P³c0 + P·P^c1·c2 + Pc3/(c4·exp(Pc5)+1) + P^c1·c6 + c7/(c8+t)
Set c7=0, c6=0, c1=1: P³c0 + P²c2 + Pc3/(c4·exp(Pc5)+1). Matches GT.
Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 5: P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + Pc3/(c4·exp(Pc5)+1) + c6·cos(Pc7)/P⁵ + c8/P⁵
Set c6=0, c8=0, c2=0. Matches GT.
Candidate 5 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 6: All terms have denominator (c1·exp(Pc2)+1). Factor out:
[P³c0 + P³c3·exp(Pc2) + P²c4·exp(Pc2) + P²c5 + Pc6·exp(Pc2) + Pc7 + Pc8] / (c1·exp(Pc2)+1)

= [P³(c0 + c3·exp(Pc2)) + P²(c5 + c4·exp(Pc2)) + P(c7+c8 + c6·exp(Pc2))] / (c1·exp(Pc2)+1)

GT = αP³ + βP² + γP/(1 + δ·exp(-εP))

Multiply GT by (1 + δ·exp(-εP))/(1 + δ·exp(-εP)):
= [αP³(1 + δ·exp(-εP)) + βP²(1 + δ·exp(-εP)) + γP] / (1 + δ·exp(-εP))

With ε > 0, let's set c2 = ε (positive), then exp(Pc2) = exp(εP). Then 1/(1+δ·exp(-εP)) = exp(εP)/(exp(εP)+δ).

So GT numerator (times exp(εP)+δ):
αP³(exp(εP)+δ) + βP²(exp(εP)+δ) + γP
= αP³·exp(εP) + αδP³ + βP²·exp(εP) + βδP² + γP

Candidate 6 numerator: P³c3·exp(Pc2) + P³c0 + P²c4·exp(Pc2) + P²c5 + P(c6·exp(Pc2) + c7 + c8)

Matching: c3=α, c0=αδ, c4=β, c5=βδ, c6=0, c7+c8=γ, c1=δ. 

But we need c6=0 (no P·exp term in GT numerator). The P term in GT numerator is just γP (no exp). So c6=0, and c7+c8=γ. This works! But wait - there are two separate P·c terms (c7 and c8). That's fine, they just add up.
Candidate 6 verdict: [MATCH]

### Candidate 7:

GT numerator: αP³·exp(εP) + αδP³ + βP²·exp(εP) + βδP² + γP
